In the nomenclature of organic compounds, skeletal replacement based on the replacement of carbon atoms by other atoms included in the general scope of the nomenclature of organic compounds is described under the title of skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature, because the heteroatoms replacing carbon atoms are denoted by nondetachable prefixes ending in ‘a’. Skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature also includes replacement of boron atoms by other atoms, including carbon (see [P-68.1.1.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6801010301)), and the replacement of heteroatoms by other atoms, including carbon, to modify fundamental structures of natural products as described in [P-101.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P10.html#10104). Skeletal replacement denoted by methods other than ‘a’ prefixes is described for the replacement of nitrogen atoms by phosphorus and arsenic atoms in certain heterocycles (see [Table 2.9](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#t209)) and oxygen atoms by sulfur, selenium, and tellurium atoms in other specific heterocycles (see [Table 2.8](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#t208)).

This section deals primarily with skeletal replacement in hydrocarbon parent hydrides. Skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature is used in two ways:

> (a) to generate names for heterocyclic parent hydrides by replacing carbon atoms in corresponding cyclic hydrocarbons; and
>
> (b) to generate simpler names for heteroacyclic structures than those formed by following the principles of substitutive nomenclature, for example, in naming polyamines, polyethers, etc., by replacing carbon atoms in corresponding acyclic hydrocarbons.

| In previous recommendations, a heteroacyclic chain had to be terminated by carbon atoms (Rule R-2.2.3.1 in the [1993 Guide](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref2)); but in these recommendations a heterocyclic chain now may terminate on any of the following heteroatoms: P, As, Sb, Bi, Si, Ge, Sn, Pb, B, Al, Ga, In, Tl, and C (see [P-15.4.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15040301)). |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |

The selection of preferred IUPAC names involving skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature is discussed in [P-51.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P5.html#5104).

P-15.4.1 General rules

P-15.4.1.1 Nondetachable prefixes, called ‘a’ prefixes, are used to designate the replacing skeletal atoms with their standard bonding number. Those related to these recommendations are listed in [Table 1.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#t105).

Table 1.5 Skeletal replacement (‘a’) prefixes

P-15.4.1.2 For naming and numbering purposes, the following decreasing order of element seniority is followed: F > Cl > Br > I >At > O > S > Se > Te > Po > N > P > As > Sb > Bi > C > Si > Ge > Sn > Pb > B > Al > Ga > In > Tl (see [Appendix 1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/Papp1.html)). Once a structure modified by skeletal replacement (‘a’) prefixes has been named and numbered, it is considered to be a new parent hydride. As locants assigned to heteroatoms are essential, all locants must be cited as defined in [P-14.3.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#140303).

P-15.4.1.3 The symbol λ_n_ is used to describe heteroatoms having nonstandard bonding numbers ([P-14.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#140103)). In names, it is placed immediately after the locant (without an intervening hyphen) denoting the heteroatom.

Example:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504a.gif)\
6λ5-phosphaspiro\[4.5]decane (PIN)P-15.4.1.4 Anionic and cationic skeletal replacement (‘a’) prefixes used to designate anionic and cationic heteroatoms are derived from the neutral prefixes given in [Table 1.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#t105). These skeletal replacement prefixes are all preselected.

Examples:

| ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504b.gif) | ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504c.gif) | ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504d.gif) |
| :-----------------------------------------------------: | :-----------------------------------------------------: | :-----------------------------------------------------: |
|                       phosphanida                       |                        boranuida                        |            <p>sulfanuida<br>λ4-sulfanida</p>            |
| ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504e.gif) | ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504f.gif) | ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504g.gif) |
|                         azanylia                        |                         iodonia                         |                         thionia                         |

The selection of preferred IUPAC names involving ionic skeletal replacement (‘a’) prefixes is fully discussed in [P-72.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#7204) and [P-73.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#7304).

P-15.4.2 Skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature is applied in three ways in naming heterocyclic parent hydrides.

P-15.4.2.1 Skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature is applied simply in the generation of individual heteromonocyclic parent hydrides (see [P-22.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#220203)), heterocyclic von Baeyer parent hydrides (see [P-23.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2303)), heterocyclic spiro parent hydrides composed of only monocyclic rings (see [P-24.2.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#24020401)), and fullerenes (see [P-27.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2705)). These heterocyclic compounds are used as identical parent structures in multiplicative nomenclature, but not as components in fusion nomenclature or ring assemblies.

P-15.4.2.2 When individual heterocycles are components of heterocyclic spiro ring systems not covered in [P-15.4.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15040201) above \[see [P-24.3.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#240304), [P-24.4.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#240403) (in part), and [P-24.5.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#240502) (in part)], heterocyclic phane systems (see [P-26.5.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#260502)), or heterocyclic ring assemblies (see [P-28.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2804)), skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature is applied in a two-step procedure. First the structure is named as a total or partial hydrocarbon system. Then skeletal replacement (‘a’) prefixes are added and cited at the front of the name. Names formed by this method are used as identical parent structures in multiplicative nomenclature.

P-15.4.2.3 Heteromonocyclic mancude components named by skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature are modified when used as component rings in fusion nomenclature \[see [P-25.2.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25020201), [P-25.2.2.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25020204) (in part), and [P-25.3.2.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2503020102)]

P-15.4.3 Skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature for acyclic parent hydrides

P-15.4.3.1 Skeletal replacement names are formed by placing skeletal replacement (‘a’) prefixes in front of the name of the unbranched parent structure in accord with their seniority order given in [P-15.4.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15040102). Multiplicative prefixes ‘di’, ‘tri’, ‘tetra’, etc, indicate a multiplicity of identical heteroatoms, and locants are used to designate their positions. The chain must be terminated by a C atom or one of the following heteroatoms: P, As, Sb, Bi, Si, Ge, Sn, Pb, B, Al, Ga, In, or Tl.

| Termination of a hetero acyclic chain by P, As, Sb, Bi, Si, Ge, Sn, Pb, B, Al, Ga, In, or Tl is a change from earlier recommendations where the chain could only be terminated by carbon atoms. |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                 |

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504h.gif)\
2,8-dioxa-4,5-dithia-11-selenadodecane (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504i.gif)\
2-oxa-4-thia-1,5-disilapentane (PIN)

P-15.4.3.2 Numbering of heteroacyclic parent hydrides

P-15.4.3.2.1 Unbranched chains are numbered continuously from one end to the other so as to give a lower set of locants to heteroatoms considered together as a set without regard to kind, and then, if there is a choice, to heteroatoms cited first in the seniority order given in [P-15.4.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15040102).

| In these recommendations, skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature generates new acyclic parent hydrides whose numbering is fixed, as it is for rings and ring systems; this is a major modification to Rule C-0.6 ([ref. 1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref1)). Then suffixes, endings, and prefixes are added in accordance with this fixed numbering. |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504j.gif)\
8-thia-2,4,6-trisiladecane (PIN)\
(the locant set ‘2,4,6,8’ is lower than ‘3,5,7,9’; see [P-14.3.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#140305))

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504k.gif)\
2-oxa-4,6,8-trisilanonane (PIN)\
(the heteroatom locant sets, ‘2,4,6,8‘, are identical;\
therefore, the low locant is given to ‘O’ over ‘Si’; see [Appendix 1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/Papp1.html))

P-15.4.3.2.2 Free valences of substituent groups receive locants according to the fixed numbering of the heterochain.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504l.gif)\
2,4,6,8-tetrasiladecan-10-yl (preferred prefix)\
\[Note the use of ‘decan-10-yl’ not ‘dec-10-yl’; see [P-29.3.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#29030202)]

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504m.gif)\
2,4,6,8-tetrasiladecan-5-yl (preferred prefix)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504n.gif)\
2,4,6,8-tetrasilaundecan-11-yl (preferred prefix)

P-15.4.3.2.3 Characteristic groups cited as suffixes are given locants in accordance with the fixed numbering of the heterochain.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504o.gif)\
2,4,6,8-tetrasilanonan-1-oic acid (PIN)\
(locant 1 is not omitted, in accordance with [P-15.4.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1504030201))

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504p.gif)\
2,4,6,8-tetrasiladecan-10-ol (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504q.gif)\
2,4,6,8-tetrasiladecan-10-oic acid (PIN)

P-15.4.3.2.4 Double and triple bonds are given locants in accordance with the fixed numbering of the heterochain, and, if there is a choice, according to the general priorities for multiple bonds (see [P-31.1.2.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P3.html#3101020202)).

Example:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504r.gif)\
2,4,6,8-tetrasiladec-9-ene (PIN)P-15.4.3.2.5 Heteroatoms with nonstandard valences

> (a) A nonstandard bonding number of a neutral skeletal heteroatom in a parent hydride is indicated by the symbol λ_n_, where ‘_n_’ is the bonding number following the appropriate locant (see [P-14.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#140103)).
>
> Example:
>
> ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504s.gif)\
> 2,5,8-trioxa-11λ4-thiadodecane (PIN)\
> (‘O’ is preferred to ‘S’ for low locant; see [Appendix 1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/Papp1.html))(b) When there is a choice, low locants are assigned to heteroatoms having a higher bonding number.
>
> Example:
>
> ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1504t.gif)\
> 2λ4,5,8,11-tetrathiadodecane (PIN)

P-15.4.3.3 The use of anionic and cationic skeletal replacement (‘a’) prefixes is fully discussed in [P-72.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#7204) and [P-73.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#7304), respectively.

P-15.5 FUNCTIONAL REPLACEMENT NOMENCLATURE

> [P-15.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#150501) Definition\
> [P-15.5.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#150502) General methodology\
> [P-15.5.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#150503) Scope of functional replacement nomenclature

P-15.5.1 Definition

Functional replacement nomenclature is a method by which oxygen atoms of characteristic groups and in functional parent compounds are replaced by halogen, chalcogen, and/or nitrogen atoms.

P-15.5.2 General methodology

The replacement of oxygen atoms or hydroxy groups by other atoms or groups can be described by nondetachable prefixes attached to, or infixes inserted into, names of characteristic groups, parent hydrides and functional parent compounds having retained or systematic names. A list of prefixes and infixes is given in [Table 1.6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#t106). Prefixes and infixes are used for designating the replacing atom(s) –OO–, –S–, –Se–, –Te–, etc. For example, thio indicates the replacement of oxygen atoms by sulfur in the suffixes sulfonothioyl and carbothioyl and in the functional parent thioacetic acid. Similarly, peroxo or peroxy indicates the replacement of an oxygen atom by the –OO– group in the suffix peroxoic acid and in the name peroxyacetic acid. When two or more prefixes or infixes are present indicating the presence of two or more different replacement groups, they are cited in names in alphabetical order, for example, cyclohexanecarboselenothioic _S_e-acid (see [P-65.1.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010501)) and 3-amido-2-imidodiphosphonic chloride (see [P-67.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#670203)).

P-15.5.3 Scope of functional replacement nomenclature

Prefixes and infixes given in [Table 1.6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#t106) are used in accordance with specific rules describing replacement in:

> [P-15.5.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15050301) Replacement in heterocyclic parent hydrides\
> [P-15.5.3.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15050302) Replacement in characteristic groups expressed as suffixes in substitutive nomenclature\
> [P-15.5.3.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15050303) Replacement in characteristic groups expressed as prefixes in substitutive nomenclature\
> [P-15.5.3.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15050304) Replacement in functional parent compounds

P-15.5.3.1 Replacement in heterocyclic parent hydrides

Prefixes are used to modify a limited group of parent hydrides as follows. See [Table 2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#t202) for pyran, [Table 2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#t203) for morpholine, [Table 2.8](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#t208) for chromene, isochromene and xanthene, and [Table 3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P3.html#t301) for chromane and isochromane.

Example:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1505a.gif)\
4_H_-thiopyran (PIN)\
4_H_-thiineP-15.5.3.2 Replacement in characteristic groups expressed as suffixes in substitutive nomenclature.

Replacement in suffixes is limited to –OO–, =S and –S–, =Se and –Se–, =Te and –Te–, =NH and =NNH2 and any combination of these affixes (see [Table 1.6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#t106)). Suffixes including a carbon atom and those corresponding to sulfonic and sulfinic acids and their analogues are modified by infixes. Other suffixes are modified by prefixes. For examples and the order of seniority of suffixes modified by functional replacement see [Tables 4.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P4.html#t402) and [4.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P4.html#t403) (Chapter [P-4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P4.html)), respectively.

Table 1.6 Prefixes and infixes in functional replacement nomenclature

\* Selenium and tellurium analogues are named using ‘seleno’ and ‘telluroְ in place of ‘thioְ.

Examples:–CO-OOH\
carboperoxoic acid (preferred suffix)

–CO-SH\
carbothioic _S_-acid (preferred suffix)

–CS-OH\
carbothioic _O_-acid (preferred suffix)

–C(=NH)-OH\
carboximidic acid (preferred suffix)

–SO-OOH\
sulfinoperoxoic acid (preselected suffix)

–S(=NNH2)-OH\
sulfinohydrazonic acid (preselected suffix)

–(C)O-SH\
thioic acid (preferred suffix)

–(C)S-NH2\
thioamide (preferred suffix; no contraction to thiamide)

\=S\
thione (preselected suffix)

–SeH\
selenol (preselected suffix)

P-15.5.3.3 Replacement in characteristic groups expressed as prefixes in substitutive nomenclature

Functional replacement is used to modify prefixes containing oxygen atoms by the prefixes ‘thio’, ‘seleno’, and ‘telluro’. Prefixes are described in appropriate sections of Chapter [P-6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html) and listed in [Appendix 2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/Papp2.html).

Examples:

–C{O/S}H\
thiocarboxy (preferred prefix)

\=S\
thioxo\
sulfanylidene (preselected prefix)

P-15.5.3.4 Replacement in functional parent compounds

Functional replacement is used to modify carboxylic acids and oxoacids, by prefixes and suffixes according to specific rules given in [P-15.5.3.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1505030401) and [P-15.5.3.4.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1505030402) below. It is also used to modify two retained names expressing functional parent structures, urea and semicarbazone, as described in [P-15.5.3.4.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1505030403) below. Functional replacement is not used to replace oxygen atoms in ketones, alcohols, or derivatives such as acetals and ketals, etc.; systematic names are recommended instead.

Examples:

CH3-CS-CH3\
propane-2-thione (PIN)\
(not thioacetone)

C6H5-SH\
benzenethiol (PIN)\
(not thiophenol)

P-15.5.3.4.1 In general nomenclature, retained names of monocarboxylic acids may be modified by the prefixes peroxy, thio, seleno, and telluro to indicate the replacement of an oxygen atom by the replacing atom(s) –OO–, –S– or =S, –Se– or =Se, and –Te– or =Te (see [P-65.1.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010401) and [P-65.1.5.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010502)).

Examples:

CH3-CO-SH\
thioacetic _S_-acid\
ethanethioic _S_-acid (PIN)

CH3-CH2-CS-OH\
thiopropionic _O_-acid\
propanethioic _O_-acid (PIN)

C6H5-CS-SH\
dithiobenzoic acid\
benzenecarbodithioic acid (PIN)

P-15.5.3.4.2 Names of mononuclear and polynuclear oxoacids are modified by prefixes and infixes listed in [Table 1.6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#t106) according to the rules described in [P-67](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#67).

Example:

CH3-P(=NH)(OH)(SH)\
_P_-methylphosphonimidothioic acid (PIN)P-15.5.3.4.3 Retained names of acyclic polynitrogen functional parent compounds described in [P-66.1.6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#660106) and [P-68.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#680301) are modified by prefixes ‘thio’, ‘seleno’, and ‘telluro’.

Examples:

H2N-CS-NH2\
thiourea (PIN; [P-66.1.6.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6601060103))\
carbonothioic diamide

H2N-NH-CSe-NH2\
selenosemicarbazide\
hydrazinecarboselenoamide (PIN, see [P-68.3.1.2.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6803010204))

P-15.6 CONJUNCTIVE NOMENCLATURE

P-15.6.0 Introduction

Conjunctive nomenclature is based essentially on the conjunctive operation, by which a compound is formally constructed by subtracting the same number of hydrogen atoms from each component at each site where joined. It is traditionally reserved for naming compounds having a principal group attached to an acyclic component that is also directly attached by a carbon-carbon bond to a cyclic component. This method can be used in general nomenclature as an alternative to substitutive nomenclature, but it is not recommended for generating preferred IUPAC names (see [P-51.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P5.html#5105)). The names have been modified ([ref. 2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref2)) so that the placement of locants in the conjunctive names is consistent with the placement of locants in names as established in these recommendations (see [P-14.3.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#140302)). Other aspects of conjunctive nomenclature used in CAS index nomenclature are discussed here briefly, including its limitations ([P-15.6.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#150602)).

P-15.6.1 Name formation

P-15.6.1.1 Names are formed by juxtaposition of component names. The name of the cyclic component is cited first followed by the systematic or retained name of the component to which the principal characteristic group is attached.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506a.gif)\
cyclohexanemethanol\
cyclohexylmethanol (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506b.gif)\
benzeneacetic acid\
phenylacetic acid (PIN)

P-15.6.1.2 When necessary, the position of attachment of the side chain to the cyclic component is given by the appropriate locant placed before the name of the cyclic component, unless locants for structural features referring to the cyclic component, such as heteroatoms and indicated hydrogen, are already there; in this case the locant follows the name of the cyclic component. Since the acyclic component must terminate at the cyclic component, it is not necessary to give its locant of attachment. Carbon atoms of the side chain are indicated by Greek letters proceeding from the principal characteristic group to the cyclic component; these locants are used in the name only to locate other substituents on the side chain. The carbon atom of the characteristic group (in acids, aldehydes, nitriles, etc.) is omitted when allocating Greek letter locants.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506c.gif)\
naphthalene-2-propanol\
3-(naphthalen-2-yl)propan-1-ol (PIN)\
3-(2-naphthyl)propan-1-ol

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506d.gif)\
1,3-thiazole-2-acetic acid\
(1,3-thiazol-2-yl)acetic acid (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506e.gif)\
β-chloronaphthalene-2-propanol\
2-chloro-3-(naphthalen-2-yl)propan-1-ol (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506f.gif)\
5,6-dimethyl-2_H_-isoindole-2-acetic acid\
(5,6-dimethyl-2_H_-isoindol-2-yl)acetic acid (PIN)

P-15.6.1.3 For all purposes in conjunctive nomenclature the side chain is considered to extend only from the principal group to the cyclic component. Any other chain members, even those extending the side chain terminally, are named as substituents, appropriate prefixes and locants being placed before the name of the cyclic component.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506g.gif)\
γ-methylnaphthalene-2-propanol\
3-(naphthalen-2-yl)butan-1-ol (PIN)\
3-(2-naphthyl)butan-1-ol

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506h.gif)\
α-propylbenzenepropanol\
1-phenylhexan-3-ol (PIN)

P-15.6.1.4 When a cyclic component carries at least two identical side chains, multiplicative prefixes ‘di’, ‘tri’, etc., are used to indicate their number; these prefixes are placed before the name of the side chain and superscript arabic numbers are used for all locants on the side chain instead of primes.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506i.gif)\
naphthalene-2,3-diacetic acid\
2,2′-(naphthalene-2,3-diyl)diacetic acid (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506j.gif)\
benzene-1,3,5-triacetic acid\
2,2′,2′′-(benzene-1,3,5-triyl)triacetic acid (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506k.gif)\
pyridine-2,3-di(decanoic acid)\
10,10′-(pyridine-2,3-diyl)di(decanoic acid) (PIN)

P-15.6.1.5 When different side chains are attached to a cyclic component:

> (a) the chain that contains the principal characteristic group is chosen for naming by the conjunctive method; or
>
> (b) if there is more than one side chain containing the principal characteristic group, the conjunctive name that expresses the greater number of the principal characteristic group is chosen. When necessary, side chains are selected by applying the seniority order for selecting the principal chain (see [P-44.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P4.html#4403)).

Examples:![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506l.gif)\
2-(3-hydroxypropyl)quinoline-3-acetic acid\
\[2-(3-hydroxypropyl)quinolin-3-yl]acetic acid (PIN)\
(a carboxylic acid is senior to an alcohol)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506m.gif)\
1-(2-carboxyethyl)naphthalene-2,3-diacetic acid\
3-\[2,3-bis(carboxymethyl)naphthalen-1-yl]propanoic acid (PIN)

P-15.6.1.6 When the side chain is linked to two different cyclic components, the senior ring or ring system is selected in accord with the seniority order of rings and ring systems (see [P-44.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P4.html#4402)).

Example:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506n.gif)\
β-cyclohexylnaphthalene-2-ethanol\
(naphthalene is senior to cyclohexane)\
2-cyclohexyl-2-(naphthalen-2-yl)ethan-1-ol (PIN)P-15.6.2 Limitations of conjunctive nomenclature

Conjunctive nomenclature is not used when:

> (a) a double bond links the acyclic component to the ring system;
>
> (b) a double bond or a heteroatom is present in the side chain;
>
> (c) two identical characteristic groups are located on the side chain provided that the condition of maximum number of principal characteristic groups is not violated;
>
> (d) characteristic groups having higher priority for citation as principal group are directly attached to the cyclic component;
>
> (e) two or more characteristic groups of the same kind as the principal group are located on the ring or ring system.

In the cases listed above, normal substitutive nomenclature must be used.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506o.gif)\
cyclopentylideneacetic acid (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506p.gif)\
phenylcarbamic acid (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506q.gif)\
2-cyclohexylhexanedioic acid (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506r.gif)\
2-(hydroxymethyl)benzene-1,4-diol (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506s.gif)\
β1,5-dihydroxybenzene-1,3-diethanol\
1-\[3-hydroxy-5-(2-hydroxyethyl)phenyl]ethane-1,2-diol (PIN)

P-15.6.3 Analysis of conjunctive name constructionNote: The PIN is the substitutive name.Example 1:![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506t.gif)Analysis:

| Principal group                                         | –OH                    | ol                      |
| ------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------- | ----------------------- |
|                                                         |                        |                         |
| Parent:                                                 |                        |                         |
|       ring:                                             | C6H6                   | benzene                 |
|       chain:                                            | CH3-CH2-CH3            | propane                 |
| Conjunctive parent including suffix:                    |                        |                         |
| ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506u.gif) |                        | benzenepropanol         |
| Prefix:                                                 | –CH2-CH2-OH            |                         |
| Prefix components:                                      | <p>–OH<br>–CH2-CH3</p> | <p>hydroxy<br>ethyl</p> |
|                                                         |                        |                         |
| Prefix name                                             |                        | 2-hydroxyethyl          |

Together with other rules, this analysis leads to the conjunctive name:

4-(2-hydroxyethyl)benzenepropanol\
3-\[4-(2-hydroxyethyl)phenyl]propan-1-ol (PIN)Example 2:![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506v.gif)

| Principal group                                         | –CHO  | carbaldehyde or al |
| ------------------------------------------------------- | ----- | ------------------ |
|                                                         |       |                    |
| Parent:                                                 |       |                    |
|                                                         | ring  | benzene            |
|                                                         | chain | heptane            |
| Conjunctive parent including suffix:                    |       |                    |
| ![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1506w.gif) |       | benzeneheptanal    |
| Prefix:                                                 | –CHO  | formyl             |

Together with other rules, this analysis leads to the conjunctive name:

3-formylbenzeneheptanal\
3-(7-oxoheptyl)benzaldehyde (PIN)P-16 NAME WRITING

> [P-16.0](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1600) Introduction\
> [P-16.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1601) Spelling\
> [P-16.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1602) Punctuation\
> [P-16.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1603) Multiplicative prefixes and ‘di’, ‘tri’, etc. _vs_. ‘bis’, ‘trisְ, etc.\
> [P-16.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1604) Other numerical terms\
> [P-16.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1605) Enclosing marks\
> [P-16.6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1606) Italicization\
> [P-16.7](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1607) Elision of vowels\
> [P-16.8](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1608) Addition of vowels\
> [P-16.9](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1609) Primes

P-16.0 INTRODUCTION

Names are written in accordance with a symbolism specific to the nomenclature of organic compounds in order to avoid ambiguity and to establish an unequivocal relationship between a name and the corresponding structure. The recommended symbolism is particularly important in the formation of IUPAC preferred names. As usual, IUPAC recognizes the needs of other languages to introduce modifications specific to a particular language, but it is hoped that, whenever possible, the following conventions will be applied to construct IUPAC names for general use as well as for IUPAC preferred names.

In the 1979 and 1993 recommendations, names were written with a capital initial letter. This practice has been abandoned in recent publications in order to ensure that names of organic compounds are not considered as proper nouns; the usual practice of capitalizing letters at the beginning of a sentence must however be respected.

P-16.1 SPELLING

The spelling of elements is that given in the IUPAC _Nomenclature of Inorganic Chemistry_ ([ref. 12](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref12), Table I, pp. 248-249), for example, sulfur not sulphur, aluminium not aluminum, and caesium not cesium.

P-16.2 PUNCTUATION

> [P-16.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160201) Commas\
> [P-16.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160202) Full stops\
> [P-16.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160203) Colons and semicolons\
> [P-16.2.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160204) Hyphens\
> [P-16.2.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160205) Spaces\
>

P-16.2.1 Commas are used:

> (a) to separate locants, numerals, or italicized letters;
>
> Examples:
>
> 1,2-dibromoethane (PIN, [P-61.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610301))
>
> _N_,_N_-diethylfuran-2-carboxamide (PIN, [P-66.1.1.3.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#660101030101))
>
> (b) to separate numbers, as well as italicized letters, in fusion descriptors when they indicate the presence of separate attached components; however, italicized letters denoting peri-fused junctions are not separated by commas.
>
> Examples:
>
> dibenzo\[_c_,_g_]phenanthrene \[PIN, [P-25.3.4.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2503040201) (c)]
>
> 6_H_-pyrrolo\[3,2,1-_de_]acridine (PIN, [P-25.3.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030103))

P-16.2.2 Full stops

Full stops are used to separate numbers that denote lengths of bridges in polyalicyclic names constructed according to the von Baeyer system (see [P-23.2.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#23020501)) and of chain lengths between spiro atoms in von Baeyer spiro names (see [P-24.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#240201)).

Examples:

bicyclo\[3.2.1]octane (PIN, [P-23.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#230203))

6-oxaspiro\[4.5]decane (PIN, [P-24.2.4.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2402040101))

P-16.2.3 Colons and semicolons

Colons separate related sets of locants; if a higher level of separation is required, semicolons are used.

Examples:

benzo\[1′′,2′′:3,4;4′′,5′′:3,4]dicyclobuta\[1,2-_b_:1′,2′-_c_′]difuran (PIN, see [P-25.3.7.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030703))

11,21:22,31-tercyclopropane (PIN, see [P-28.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#280301))

P-16.2.4 Hyphens

P-16.2.4.1 Hyphens are used in substitutive names:

> (a) to separate locants from words or word fragments;
>
> Example:
>
> 2-chloro-2-methylpropane (PIN, [P-61.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610301))(b) after parentheses, if the closing parenthesis is followed by a locant;
>
> Examples:
>
> 1-(chloromethyl)-4-nitrobenzene (PIN, [P-61.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610501))
>
> _N_1-(2-aminoethyl)-_N_1,_N_2,_N_2 -trimethylethane-1,2-diamine (PIN, [P-62.2.4.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6202040103))
>
> (c) to separate adjacent locants from a subsequent opening enclosing mark;
>
> Examples:
>
> 1-(3,4-dihydroquinolin-1(2_H_)-yl)ethan-1-one (PIN, [P-64.3.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#640302))
>
> _N_-acetyl-_N_-(3-chloropropanoyl)benzamide (PIN, [P-66.1.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66010201))
>
> (d) to separate italic letters from Roman letters;
>
> Examples:
>
> di-_tert_-butyl ([P-61.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610203))
>
> _as_-indacene ([P-25.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#250101))

P-16.2.4.2 No hyphen is placed after a numerical prefix cited in front of a compound substituent enclosed by parentheses, even if that substituent begins with locants;

Example:

_N_,1-bis(4-chlorophenyl)methanimine (PIN, [P-62.3.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#62030101))P-16.2.4.3 Hyphens separate the two parts of a fusion descriptor, i.e., numbers and italicized letters.

Example:

naphtho\[1,2-_a_]azulene (PIN, [P-25.3.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030103))P-16.2.4.4 Hyphens separate stereodescriptors from the rest of the name or the part of a name to which they relate.

Example:

(2_E_)-but-2-ene (PIN, [P-93.4.2.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#9304020101))P-16.2.4.5 A long hyphen (an ‘em’ dash) is used to separate the names of components in adducts.

Example:

carbon monoxide—methylborane (PIN, [P-13.3.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#130305))P-16.2.5 Spaces are a very important type of punctuation for many kinds of names in the English language. If a space is required in a name, it must be used. On the other hand, the use of spaces where they are not required, for example, in substitutive names that must be written continuously from one end to the other using hyphens to connect the different parts, may be misleading. Spaces are used in:

> (a) names of acids and salts;
>
> Examples:
>
> acetic acid (PIN, [P-65.1.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010101))
>
> sodium 4-ethoxy-4-oxobutanoate (PIN, [P-65.6.3.3.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6506030305))
>
> (b) functional class names;
>
> Examples:
>
> ethyl acetate (PIN, [P-65.6.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6506030201))
>
> 2-(carbonocyanidothioyl)benzoyl chloride (PIN, [P-65.5.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#650504))
>
> butyl ethyl sulfoxide [(P-63.6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6306))\
> 1-(ethanesulfinyl)butane (PIN)
>
> (c) names formed using a functional modifier;
>
> Examples:
>
> cyclohexanone ethyl methyl ketal ([P-66.6.5.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6606050101))\
> 1-ethoxy-1-methoxycyclohexane (PIN)
>
> pentan-2-one oxime ([P-68.3.1.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6803010102))\
> (pentan-2-ylidene)hydroxylamine\
> _N_-hydroxypentan-2-imine (PIN)
>
> (d) additive names;
>
> Examples:
>
> ethene oxide ([P-63.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6305))\
> oxirane (PIN)
>
> trimethylphosphane oxide\
> trimethyl-λ5-phosphanone (PIN, [P-68.3.2.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6803020301), [P-74.2.1.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#74020104))

P-16.3 MULTIPLICATIVE PREFIXES ‘DI’, ‘TRI’, ETC. _vs_.‘BIS’, ‘TRIS’, ETC.

P-16.3.1 Multiplicative prefixes are derived from Greek and Latin number names (see [P-14.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1402)) and are the principal method for describing a multiplicity of identical features of a structure in chemical names. They are intimately interconnected with enclosing marks, particularly parentheses.

P-16.3.2 General methodology.

The general method to best determine whether ‘di’, ‘tri’, etc. or ‘bis’, ‘tris’, etc. should be used involves the following steps, not necessarily in the order given:

> (a) determine whether the component to be multiplied is simple or compound. Simple components are unsubstituted parent hydrides, such as naphthalene ; unsubstituted prefixes, such as ethyl or _tert_-butyl; functionalized parent hydrides, such as benzenesulfonic acid; or retained names, such as acetic acid. All of these are multiplied by the multiplicative prefixes ‘di’, ‘tri’, etc.;
>
> (b) determine whether these simple nomenclatural components require parentheses (see [P-16.3.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160304)) and insert them into the name;
>
> (c) any component which is substituted automatically requires use of the multiplicative forms ‘bis’, ‘tris’, etc.;
>
> (d) determine whether a simple nomenclature component would be ambiguous if multiplied by the multiplicative prefixes ‘di’, ‘tri’, etc., with or without the parentheses (see [P-16.3.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160304)).

P-16.3.3 The basic numerical prefixes ‘di’, ‘tri’, ‘tetra’, etc. are used to indicate a multiplicity of:

> (a) functional and cumulative suffixes, basic or modified by functional replacement, with the exception of ‘thioic acid’ and ‘dithioic acid’ described in [P-16.3.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160305) (b);
>
> Examples:
>
> diol (see [P-63.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#630102))
>
> dicarboxylic acid (see [P-65.1.1.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6501010201))
>
> disulfonic acid (see [P-65.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#650301))
>
> diyl (see [P-71.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#710203))
>
> diide (see [P-72.2.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#72020201))
>
> diium (see [P-73.1.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#73010102))
>
> diperoxoic acid (see [P-65.1.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010401))
>
> dicarboperoxoic acid (see [P-65.1 4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010401))
>
> diimidic acid ([P-65.1.3.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6501030101))
>
> dicarbohydrazonic acid ([P-65.1.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6501030201))
>
> disulfonoperoxoic acid (see [P-65.3.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65030102))
>
> disulfinimidic acid (see [P-65.3.1.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65030104))
>
> disulfonohydrazonimidic acid (see [P-65.3.1.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65030104))
>
> dithioamide (see [P-66.1.4.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6601040101))
>
> diimidamide (see [P-66.4.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66040101))
>
> dicarbohydrazonamide ([P-66.4.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66040201))
>
> dicarboximidohydrazide ([P-66.4.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66040201))
>
> dicarboximidamide (see [P-66.4.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66040101))
>
> (b) simple substituent prefixes, including parent hydrides with ‘ene’ and ‘yne’ endings (without locants), and characteristic groups
>
> Examples:
>
> dicyclohexyl (see [P-44.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P4.html#440102))
>
> dimethyl (see [P-61.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610203))
>
> di-_tert_-butyl (see [P-61.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610203))
>
> diethenyl (see [P-61.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610203))
>
> diimino (see [P-62.3.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#62030102))
>
> dibromo (see [P-61.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610301))
>
> (c) skeletal ‘a’ replacement prefixes
>
> Examples:
>
> trisila (see [P-15.4.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1504030201))
>
> trioxa (see [P-15.4.3.2.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1504030205))
>
> (d) multiplied components with retained names and systematic names other than those described in [P-16.3.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160304) (c), [P-16.3.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160304) (d) and [P-16.3.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160304) (e).
>
> Examples:
>
> diphenol (see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))
>
> diacetic acid (see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201); see also [P-15.6.1.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15060104))
>
> dipropanoic acid (see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))
>
> (e) simple functional modifiers
>
> Examples:
>
> dioxime (see [P-68.3.1.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6803010102))
>
> dihydrazide (see [P-66.3.5.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66030502))

P-16.3.4 Parentheses (round brackets) (see [P-16.6.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160601)) are used to enclose multiplied components that are:

> (a) simple substituent prefixes having locants;
>
> Examples:
>
> di(propan-2-yl) (preferred prefix; see [P-61.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610203))
>
> tetra(naphthalen-2-yl) (preferred prefix; see [P-61.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610203))
>
> (b) simple substituent prefixes modified by ‘ene’ and ‘yne’ endings and that have locants;
>
> Example:
>
> di(prop-1-en-2-yl) (preferred prefix; see [P-68.2.6.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#68020601))(c) simple substituent prefixes and functionalized parent hydrides beginning with a multiplicative prefix;

| This is a change from earlier editions where ‘bi’ was used |
| ---------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                            |

> Examples:
>
> di(dodecyl) (preferred prefix; see [P-68.2.6.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#68020601))
>
> di(tridecyl) (preferred prefix, see [P-52.2.8](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P5.html#520208))
>
> di(tetradecane-14,1-diyl) (multipicative preferred prefix: see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))
>
> di(pentanal) (see [P-68.2.6.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#68020602))
>
> (d) simple substituent groups and functionalized parent hydrides beginning with ‘dec’ to distinguish multiplied groups from acyclic components containing 12 to 19 atoms (see [P-15.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#150102))
>
> Examples:
>
> di(decyl) (see [P-57.1.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P5.html#57010101))
>
> di(decanoic acid) (see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))
>
> tri(decyl) \[preferred prefix,\
> defines three –C10H21 groups, see [P-61.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610203),\
> tridecyl defines the –C13H27 group, see [P-57.1.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P5.html#57010101)]
>
> tetra(decanoic acid) (preferred suffix,\
> defines four decanoic acid suffixes;\
> tetradecanoic acid defines an acid suffix group with fourteen atoms)
>
> (e) functionalized parent hydrides with locants;
>
> Examples:
>
> di(benzene-1-sulfonic acid) (see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))
>
> di(cyclohexane-1-carboxylic acid) (see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))
>
> (f) simple components containing brackets;
>
> Examples:
>
> 8,8′-oxydi(spiro\[4.5]decane) (PIN; see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))
>
> di(bicyclo\[3.2.1]octan-3-yl) (preferred prefix; see [P-44.2.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P4.html#44020101))
>
> di(\[4-2H]benzoyl) (preferred prefix, see [P-83.1.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P8.html#83010202))

P-16.3.5 The numerical prefixes ‘bis’, ‘tris’, ‘tetrakis’, etc. are used to indicate a multiplicity of:

> (a) compound or complex (i.e. substituted) prefixes (see [P-35.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P3.html#3503) and [P-35.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P3.html#3504));
>
> Examples:
>
> bis(2-chloropropan-2-yl) (preferred prefix; see [P-61.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610301))
>
> bis(dimethylamino) (preferred prefix; see [P-62.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6205))
>
> ethane-1,2-diylbis(oxymethylene) (preferred prefix; see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))
>
> bis(bromomethyl) (preferred prefix, see [P-61.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610301))
>
> (b) ‘thioic acid’ and ‘dithioic acid’ suffixes, and their Se and Te analogues, as exceptions to suffixes described in [P-16.3.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160303) and [P-16.3.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160304);
>
> Examples:
>
> bis(thioic acid) \[multiple preferred suffix,\
> describes two –C(O/S)H suffixes, see [P-65.1.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010501);\
> whereas dithioic acid describes a –CSSH suffix, see [P-65.1.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010501)]
>
> bis(dithioic acid) (multiple preferred suffix,\
> describes two –CSSH suffixes, see [P-65.1.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010501))\
> not didithoic acid
>
> (c) before suffixes that are composed of two or more cumulative suffixes;
>
> Examples:
>
> bis(ylium) (multiple preferred suffix,\
> describes two ‘-ylium’ suffixes, see [P-73.2.2.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#7302020102);\
> whereas ‘diylium’ could describe a cation radical suffix)
>
> bis(nitrilium) (preferred suffix,\
> describes two ‘nitrilium’ suffixes, see [P-73.1.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#73010201);\
> whereas ‘dinitrilium’ might be interpreted as two ‘nitrile’ suffixes and one ‘ium’ suffix)
>
> (d) substituted functional modifiers;
>
> Examples:
>
> bis(phenylhydrazone) (see [P-68.3.1.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6803010202))
>
> pentane-2,4-dione bis(_O_-phenyloxime) (see [P-68.3.1.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6803010102))
>
> (e) substituted parent compounds in multiplicative nomenclature.
>
> Examples:
>
> bis(2-bromobenzoic acid) (see [P-15.3.2.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1503020401))
>
> bis\[5-(1-chloroethyl)pyridine] (see [P-15.3.2.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1503020401))

P-16.3.6 The prefixes ‘bis’, ‘tris’, ‘tetrakis’, etc. are also used to avoid ambiguity:

> (a) before a mononuclear subset of a polynyclear acyclic structure;
>
> Examples:
>
> bis(sulfanyl) (preferred prefix;\
> defines two –SH groups, see [P-63.1.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#630105);\
> whereas disulfanyl defines the –SSH group; see [P-63.4.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#63040202))
>
> tris(sulfanyl) (preferred prefix;\
> defines three –SH groups (see [P-63.1.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#630105))]\
> whereas trisulfanyl (preferred prefix; defines the –SSSH group; see [P-68.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#680401))
>
> bis(λ4-sulfanyl) (preferred prefix;\
> defines two –SH3 groups) (not di(λ4-sulfanyl)
>
> Note: And similarly for the analogous Se, Te, N, P, As, Sb, Bi, Si, Ge, Sn, Pb, B, Al, Ga, In, and Tl groups.bis(phosphonic acid) \[preselected name;\
> describes two phosphonic acids, see [P-67.1.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#67010102);\
> diphosphonic acid describes the acid (HO)(O)PH-O-PH(O)(OH), see [P-67.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#670201))]
>
> bis(hydrogen sulfate) \[preselected name;\
> describes two (hydrogen sulfate) anions or acid esters, see [P-67.1.3.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#67010302),\
> hydrogensulfate is an inorganic name for HSO4–, see [ref. 12](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref12), IR 8.5]
>
> tris(iodide) \[preselected name\
> describes three iodide ions, see [ref. 12](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref12), IR 5.4.2.3;\
> triiodide describes the (I3–) anion; see [ref. 12](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref12), IR 5.4.2.3]
>
> bis(phosphate) (preselected name)\
> Example: D-fructofuranose 1,6-bis(phosphate) (see [P-102.5.6.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P10.html#10205060102))]
>
> (b) before the retained names of mononuclear divalent substituent groups, such as ‘oxy’, ‘thio’, and ‘methylene’ to distinguish multiplied groups from chains (see [P-15.3.1.2.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#150301020201));
>
> Examples:
>
> bis(oxy) \[preferred prefix,\
> defines two –O– groups, see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201);\
> whereas ‘dioxy‘ would define the –OO– group, used in the past, see [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))]
>
> bis(methylene) \[preferred prefix,\
> defines two –CH2– groups, see [P-29.4.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#290402);\
> whereas dimethylene might be used to define the –CH2-CH2– group\
> properly named as ethane-1,2-diyl (preferred prefix) or ethylene; see [P-29.6.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#29060203)]
>
> bis(azo) defines two –N=N– groups, see [P-68.3.1.3.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#680301030203);\
> whereas ‘diazo’ is one =N2 group, see [P-61.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6104))\
> Example: 3,3′-\[methylenebis(azo)]dipropanoic acid
>
> bis(sulfonyl) (preferred prefix,\
> defines two –SO2– groups, see [P-65.3.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65030203);\
> whereas ‘disulfonyl’ is –SO2-SO2–)\
> Example: 3,3′-\[oxybis(sulfonyl)]di(propan-1-ol) (PIN; see [P-65.3.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65030203))
>
> bis(sulfinyl) (preferred prefix,\
> defines two –S(O)– groups, see [P-65.3.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65030203); disulfinyl is –S(O)-S(O)–)\
> Example: 3,3′-\[azanediylbis(sulfinyl)]di(propan-1-amine) (PIN, see [P-65.3.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65030203))
>
> (c) before skeletal replacement (‘a’) prefixes, such as ‘aza’, ‘oxa’, etc. that are used in the construction of Hantzsch-Widman names and in skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature, to describe clearly the number of replacement atoms in a name or name component;
>
> Examples:
>
> benzo\[1,2-_c_:3,4-_c_′]bis(\[1,2,5]oxadiazole) (PIN,\
> describes two ‘oxadiazole’ rings, see [P-25.3.7.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030701);\
> whereas the name ‘benzo\[1,2-_c_:3,4-_c_′]di\[1,2,5]oxadiazole’ might describe\
> a five-membered ring with two oxygen atoms and two nitrogen atoms, see [P-22.2.2.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2202020101))
>
> bis(azacyclododecane) (PIN,\
> describes two ‘azacyclododecane’ rings, see [P-22.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#220203);\
> whereas the name diazacyclododecane describes\
> a cyclododecane ring with two nitrogen atoms, see [P-22.2.3.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2202030202))
>
> bis(1,2-oxazol-3-yl) \[preferred prefix,\
> but di(isoxazol-3-yl), see [P-16.3.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160302);\
> whereas di(1,2-oxazol-3-yl) might be interpreted\
> as a ‘dioxazole’ ring system, see [P-22.2.2.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2202020101))]
>
> (d) before attached components in fusion nomenclature to distinguish a multiplicative prefix from multiplied attached fusion components;
>
> Examples:
>
> bis(benzo\[_a_]anthracen-1-yl) (preferred prefix,\
> describes two ‘benzo\[_a_]anthracen-1-yl prefixes; see [P-61.2.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#610204);\
> whereas dibenzo\[_a_]anthracen-1-yl might be interpreted\
> as a dibenzoanthracene ring system; see [P-25.3.4.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2503040201))
>
> bis(cyclobuta\[1,2-_c_]furan) (PIN,\
> describes two cyclobuta\[1,2-_c_]furan ring systems, see [P-25.3.7.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030703);\
> whereas dicyclobuta\[1,2-_c_]furan might be interpreted\
> as a dicyclobutafuran ring system, see [P-25.3.6.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030601))
>
> (e) before names beginning with a multiplicative prefix ‘di’.
>
> Examples:
>
> bis(diazonium) (preselected suffix, see [P-73.2.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#73020203)) (not didiazonium)
>
> bis(diazenyl) (preselected prefix, see [P-68.3.1.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6803010301)) (not didiazenyl)
>
> bis(disulfanyl) (preselected prefix, see [P-29.3.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#29030202), [P-63.1.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#630105), and [P-63.4.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#64040202)) (not didisulfanyl)
>
> tris(dihydrogen phosphate) (preselected name; see [P-67.1.3.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#67010302)) (not tridihydrogen phosphate)

P-16.4 OTHER NUMERICAL TERMS

P-16.4.1 The numerical prefixes ‘bi’, ‘ter’, ‘quater’, etc. are used mainly in naming ring assemblies (see [P-28](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#28)).

Examples:

1,1′-biphenyl (PIN, [P-28.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#280201))

12,22:26,32:36,42-quaterpyridine (PIN, [P-28.3.1)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#280301)

P-16.4.2 The prefix ‘mono’ is usually omitted in names of organic compounds. However, it is used to indicate that only one characteristic group of a parent structure has been modified. The ending ‘kis’ is never associated with ‘mono’.

Examples:

monoperoxyphthalic acid ([P-65.1.4.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010402))

2-carbonoperoxoylbenzoic acid (PIN; see [P-65.1.4.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010402))

carbon monoxide (PIN; see [P-13.3.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#130305))

P-16.4.3 The term ‘sesqui’ is used to mean one and a half times as great. It is not used in IUPAC names as a numerical prefix, but may be found as a general descriptive term, for example ‘sesquisiloxanes’.

P-16.5 ENCLOSING MARKS

Parentheses, ( ), (also called ‘curves’ or ‘round brackets’), brackets, \[ ], (also called ‘square brackets’), and braces { }, (also called ‘curly brackets’) are used in chemical nomenclature to set off parts of a name dealing with specific structural features in order to convey the structure of a compound as clearly as possible. It is important to note that although they are used in the same way in names of organic and inorganic compounds, they are not used in the same way in inorganic formulas.

Enclosing marks must not be omitted from preferred IUPAC names. In general nomenclature, when there is no possible ambiguity, enclosing marks may be omitted to simplify a name.

> [P-16.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160501) Parentheses (also called curves or round brackets)\
> [P-16.5.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160502) Brackets (also called square brackets)\
> [P-16.5.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160503) Braces (also called curly brackets)\
> [P-16.5.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160504) Multiple types of enclosing marks [![added heading](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

P-16.5.1 Parentheses (also called curves or round brackets)

P-16.5.1.1 Parentheses are used around compound (see [P-29.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#290102)) and complex (see [P-29.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#290103)) prefixes; after the multiplicative prefixes ‘bis’, ‘tris’, etc.; to enclose a multiplied parent compound consisting of a parent hydride and a substituent suffix or a multiplied substituent prefix even though preceded by a basic numerical prefix, such as ‘di’, ‘tri’, etc.

Examples:

Cl-CH2-SiH3\
(chloromethyl)silane \[PIN;\
the name chloro(methyl)silane would describe the structure Cl-SiH2-CH3]

(HO-CH2-CH2-O)2CH-COOH\
bis(2-hydroxyethoxy)acetic acid (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605a.gif)\
1,3,5-tri(decyl)cycohexane (PIN)\
(not 1,3,5-tris(decyl)cyclohexane)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605b.gif)\
4,4′-methylenedi(cyclohexane-1-carboxylic acid) (PIN)

H{S/O}C-CH2-CH2-C{O/S}H\
butanebis(thioic acid) (PIN)

–CH-\[CH2]12-CH2-O-CH2-\[CH2]12-CH2–\
oxydi(tetradecane-14,1-diyl) (preferred prefix;\
note the order of the substituent locants used in multiplicative nomenclature)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605c.gif)\
1,4-di(tridecyl)benzene (PIN)

P-16.5.1.2 Parentheses are used around simple substituent prefixes (see [P-29.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2901)) to separate locants of the same type referring to different structural elements, even though locants referring to a particular structural feature may not be explicitly cited. This is recommended for clarity since locants assigned to free valences were previously placed in front of the name, for example, 2-naphthyl.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605d.gif)\
(naphthalen-2-yl)acetic acid (PIN)\
(the locant ‘2’ for acetic acid is not cited, see [P-14.3.4.6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#14030406))\
naphthalene-2-acetic acid

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605e.gif)\
4-(pyridin-4-yl)benzamide (PIN)\
\[former name 4-(4-pyridinyl)benzamide]\
4-(4-pyridyl)benzamide

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605f.gif)\
(naphthalen-2-yl)(phenyl)diazene (PIN; see [P-68.3.1.3.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#680301030202))\
(2-naphthyl)phenyldiazene

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605g.gif)\
_N_-(furan-2-yl)-1_H_-pyrrol-2-amine (PIN)\
(furan-2-yl)(1_H_-pyrrol-2-yl)amine\
(2-furyl)(pyrrol-2-yl)amine

P-16.5.1.3 Parentheses for substituents of parent structures. [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

P-16.5.1.3.1 For mononuclear parent hydrides with two or more substituents the first cited substituent never has enclosing marks unless it is a compound substituent group or includes a locant. The second and further substituents are each enclosed with parentheses even for simple substituents. When the simple substituent groups are accompanied by multiplicative prefixes such as ‘di’ and ‘tri’, the multiplicative prefixes are not included in the parentheses. [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605h.gif)\
butyl(ethyl)(methyl)(propyl)silane (PIN)

CH3-SiH2Cl\
chloro(methyl)silane (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605i.gif)\
ethyl(methyl)(propyl)phosphane (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605j.gif)\
ethyl(methyl)(propan-2-yl)phosphane (PIN)\
ethyl(isopropyl)(methyl)phosphane

ClCH2-SiH2-CH3\
(chloromethyl)(methyl)silane (PIN; [P-68.2.6.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#68020601))

BrCH2-SiH2-CH2Cl\
(bromomethyl)(chloromethyl)silane (PIN; [P-68.2.6.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#68020601))

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605k.gif)\
ethyldi(methyl)phosphane (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605l.gif)\
ethyldi(propan-2-yl)silane (PIN)\
ethyldi(isopropyl)silane

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605la.gif)\
ethyl(methyl)(propyl)silanecarboxylic acid (PIN) [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605lb.gif)\
methyl(phenyl)phosphinic acid (PIN) [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605lc.gif)\
cyclopropyl(phenyl)methanol (PIN) [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

P-16.5.1.3.2 Simple substituents of a parent where only one possible position can be substituted do not require locants. Enclosing marks are used with second and subsequent simple substituents (see [P-16.5.1.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1605010301)). In some cases, such as acetic acid, alkyl substituents are not allowed as the resulting compound requires a different parent structure. Locants are required for related compounds where additional substitutable positions are available, for example acetamide.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605ld.gif)\
bromo(nitro)(phenyl)acetic acid (PIN) [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605le.gif)\
diethyl ethyl(methyl)propanedioate (PIN) [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605lf.gif)\
bromo(chloro)acetic acid (PIN) [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605lg.gif)\
cyclopropyl(fluoro)acetonitrile (PIN) [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

P-16.5.1.4 Parentheses are placed around substituent groups including the name of a parent hydride in order to avoid any confusion from having two parent hydrides in a substitutive name.

| This is a change from the 1993 Guide ([ref. 2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref2)) to facilitate name interpretation in names as such as cyclohexanecarbonyl, in that they, even though they are simple prefixes, could give the illusion that two parent hydrides are present. |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605m.gif)\
4-(cyclohexanecarbonyl)benzene-1-carbothioic acid (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605n.gif)\
di(benzenesulfinyl)acetic acid (PIN)

P-16.5.1.5 Parentheses are placed around a prefix denoting simple hydrocarbyl substituents adjacent to the term ‘amine’ in naming amines using ‘amine’ as the parent structure, when several different substituent groups are present. This requirement is necessary to insure the specificity of this kind of amine name and to distinguish them from older names. Other enclosing marks are used as needed.

Examples:

(2-chloroethyl)(propyl)amine ([P-62.2.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#62020201))\
_N_-(2-chloroethyl)propan-1-amine (PIN)

butyl(ethyl)(propyl)amine ([P-62.2.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#62020201))\
_N_-ethyl-_N_-propylbutan-1-amine (PIN)

butyl(ethyl)(methyl)amine ([P-62.2.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#62020201))\
_N_-ethyl-_N_-methylbutan-1-amine (PIN)

P-16.5.1.6 Parentheses are used to isolate a second locant of a compound locant, around locants denoting ring numbering in phane nomenclature, and to enclose fullerene identifiers.

Examples:

bicyclo\[8.5.1]hexadeca-1(15),10-diene (PIN, [P-31.1.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P3.html#31010101))

1(1,3),4(1,4)-dibenzenacycloheptaphane (PIN, [P-26.4.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#26040202))

(C60-_I_h)\[5,6]fullerene (PIN, [P-27.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#270202))

P-16.5.1.7 Parentheses are used to enclose ‘added indicated hydrogen’ and its locant, stereodescriptors such as ‘_E_’, ‘_Z_’, ‘_R_’, ‘_S_’, etc., and descriptors for isotopically substituted compounds.

Examples:

phosphinin-2(1_H_)-one (PIN, [P-14.7.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#140702))

(2_E_)-but-2-ene (PIN, [P-93.4.2.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#9304020101))

(13C)methane (PIN, [P-82.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P8.html#820201))

P-16.5.1.8 Parentheses are used to clarify a modification made by functional replacement prefixes.

Example:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605o.gif)\
4-(thioacetyl)benzoic acid\
4-(ethanethioyl)benzoic acid (PIN, [P-65.1.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65010501))P-16.5.1.9 Parentheses (or other enclosing marks if parentheses are already present) are placed around a parent structure including the prefix ‘di’ or ‘bis’ before multiparent systems ([P-25.3.7.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030701)) substituted by one substituent group only cited as suffix.

Examples:

\[benzo\[1,2-_c_:3,4-_c_′]bis(\[1,2,5]oxadiazole)]-4-carboxylic acid (PIN; [P-65.1.2.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6501020202))

(benzo\[1,2:4,5]di\[7]annulene)-2-carbonitrile (PIN; ([P-66.5.1.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6605010103))

P-16.5.1.10 Parentheses are used to enclose terms modified by the numerical prefixes ‘bis’, ‘tris’, ‘tetrakis’, etc., discussed in [P-16.3.6](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160306).

Example:

disilylmethyl (preferred prefix; see [P-68.2.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#680205))\
bis(silanyl)methylP-16.5.1.11 Parentheses are used to enclose groups attached to a chain in linear formulas.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605p.gif)\
propane-2-thiol (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605q.gif)\
3-hydroxybutan-2-one (PIN)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605r.gif)\
2,2-dimethylpentane (PIN)

P-16.5.1.12 Parentheses are used to enclose multiple dots and charges in radical ion structures.

Example:

\[C6H5-C6H5]\(2•)(2–)\
\[1,1′-biphenyl]dielide (PIN)\
biphenyl diradical\
dianion biphenyl diradical ion(2–)P-16.5.2 Brackets (also called square brackets)

P-16.5.2.1 Brackets enclose descriptors denoting fusion sites in fused ring systems and enclose numbers denoting the length of bridges and chains connecting spiro atoms in names of polyalicyclic ring systems constructed according to von Baeyer methods. They also enclose ring assembly names when these are followed by a principal group suffix or a cumulative suffix and enclose names of components in von Baeyer spiro names.

Examples:

naphtho\[2,1-_a_]azulene (PIN, [P-25.3.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030103))

bicyclo\[3.2.1]octane (PIN, [P-23.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#230202))

spiro\[4.5]decane (PIN, [P-24.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#240201))

\[2,2′-bipyridin]-5-yl (preferred prefix, [P-29.3.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#290305))

spiro\[cyclohexane-1,1′-indene] (PIN, [P-24.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#240501))

P-16.5.2.2 Brackets enclose locants that describe structural features of components, such as double bonds in bridges and heteroatoms of component rings in names of fused ring systems.

Examples:

6,7-(epiprop\[1]en\[1]yl\[3]ylidene)benzo\[_a_]cyclohepta\[_e_]\[8]annulene (PIN, [P-25.4.3.4.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2504030402))

5_H_-pyrido\[2,3-_d_]\[1,2]oxazine \[PIN, [P-25.3.2.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030204) (d)]

P-16.5.2.3 Brackets enclose the numerals that describe ring size in annulenes and fullerenes.

Examples:

\[10]annulene ([P-22.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#220102))\
cyclodeca-1,3,5,7,9-pentaene (PIN)

(C60-_I_h)\[5,6]fullerene (PIN, [P-27.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#270202))

P-16.5.2.4 Brackets enclose substituent prefixes in which parentheses have already been used.

Example:

4-\[(hydroxyselanyl)methyl]benzoic acid (PIN, [P-63.4.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#63040202))P-16.5.2.5 Brackets are used to enclose descriptors for isotopically labeled compounds.

Example:

\[13C]methane (PIN, [P-83.1.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P8.html#83010201))P-16.5.2.6 Brackets are employed in formulae to indicate repetition of a group in a chain.

Example:

CH3-\[CH2]68-CH3\
heptacontane (PIN, [P-21.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#210201))P-16.5.3 Braces (also called curly brackets)

P-16.5.3.1 Braces are used to enclose substituent prefixes in which brackets and parentheses have already been used.

Example:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605s.gif)\
2-{2-\[1-(2-aminoethoxy)ethoxy]ethoxy}propanenitrile (PIN)P-16.5.4 Multiple types of enclosing marks [![made a separate heading](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

When multiple types of enclosing marks are required, the nesting order is as follows: {\[({\[( )]})]}, etc. as illustrated in [Fig.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#t103). It must be noted, however, that the presence of square brackets and/or parentheses that are an integral part of the name of a parent structure does not affect the nesting order given here.

| <p><img src="https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605t.gif" alt=""><br>(a) = 4′-cyano[1,1′-biphenyl]-4-yl<br>(b) = (4′-cyano[1,1′-biphenyl]-4-yl)oxy<br>(c) = 5-[(4′-cyano[1,1′-biphenyl]-4-yl)oxy]pentyl<br>(d) = {5-[(4′-cyano[1,1′-biphenyl]-4-yl)oxy]pentyl}oxy<br>(e) = 3-({5-[(4′-cyano[1,1′-biphenyl]-4-yl)oxy]pentyl}oxy)-3-oxopropane-1,2-diyl<br>(f) = 4,4′-[3-({5-[(4′-cyano[1,1′-biphenyl]-4-yl)oxy]pentyl}oxy)-3-oxopropane-1,2-diyl]dibenzoic acid (PIN)<br></p> |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |

Fig. 1.3 Nesting order of enclosing marks

Example:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1605u.gif)\
2,2′-({2-\[(carboxymethyl)(2-hydroxyethyl)amino]ethyl}azanediyl)diacetic acid\
_N_-(carboxymethyl)-_N_′-(2-hydroxyethyl)-_N_,_N_′-(ethane-1,2-diyl)diglycineP-16.5.4.1 The presence of square brackets and/or parentheses that are an integral part of the name of a parent structure may affect the nesting order as described below. [![revised P-16.5.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)

P-16.5.4.1.1 In determining the nesting order in a name the parentheses of added indicated hydrogen are ignored.

Example:

1-(3,4-dihydroquinolin-1(2_H_)-yl)ethan-1-one (PIN, [P-64.3.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#640302))P-16.5.4.1.2 In determining the nesting order in a name the square brackets of ring fusion, spiro fusion, ring assembly, or the extended von Baeyer names are ignored.

Examples:

(7,7-dimethyl-2-oxobicyclo\[2.2.1]heptan-1-yl)methanesufonic acid (PIN, [P-14.8.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#140801))\
10,10′-\[\[1,1′-biphenyl]-4,4′-diylbis(oxy)]di(decanoic acid) (PIN, [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))\
trispiro{1-oxaspiro\[2.3]hexane-2,3′:4,3′′:5,3′′′-tri(tetracyclo\[3.2.0.02,7.04.6]heptane)} (PIN, [P-24.7.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#24070401))\
_N_-(dibenzo\[_b_,_d_]furan-1-yl)acetamide (PIN, [P-66.1.1.4.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6601010403))P-16.5.4.1.3 In determining the nesting order in a name the parentheses used to indicate compound locants, phane amplification locants, stereochemistry, specific isotopic substitution, or coordination with multicenter bonding are taken into consideration.

Examples:

2-\[bicyclo\[6.6.1]pentadeca-8(15)-en-1-yl]ethan-1-ol (PIN)\
trimethyl\[12_H_-1(6)-pyrana-3,5(1,4),7(1)-tribenzenaheptaphan-74-yl]silane (PIN) ([P-44.1.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P4.html#44010201))\
\[1(1′)_E_,3_E_,3′_E_-3,3′-diethylidene-1,1′-bi(cyclobutylidene) (PIN, [P-93.5.1.4.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#930501040201))\
\[1(44)_E_,2_S_,26_R_]-bicyclo\[24.20.1]heptatetraconta-1(46),44,45-trien-2-ol (PIN, [P-93.5.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#93050203))\
10-{\[(3_S_)-1-phosphabicyclo\[2.2.2]octan-3-yl]methyl}-10_H_-phenoxazine (PIN)\
(3_S_)-2-\[(2_S_)-2-{\[(1_S_)-1-ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl]amino}propanoyl]-1,2,3,4-tetrahydroisoquinoline-3-carboxylic acid (PIN)\
1,2-di\[(13C)methyl]benzene (PIN. [P-82.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P8.html#820201))\
3-\[ethyl(2-34S)trisulfanyl]propanoic acid (PIN, [P-82.6.3.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P8.html#82060302))\
\[(2,3,5,6-η)-bicyclo\[2.2.1]hepta-2,5-diene]tricarbonyliron ([P-69.2.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#690204))\
{μ-\[2(1-3,3a,8a-η):1(4-6-η)]azulene}-(pentacarbonyl-1κ3C,2κ2C)diiron(Fe—Fe) ([P-69.2.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#690205))P-16.5.4.1.4 In determining the nesting order where square brackets are used for an isotopically labelled compound, by convention, parenthesis are used.

Example:

1-(amino\[14C]methyl)cyclopentan-1-ol (PIN, [P-83.1.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P8.html#83010201))P-16.5.4.1.5 When the nesting order given in [P-16.5.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160504) results in consecutive enclosing marks of the same level, the next level of enclosing mark is used. For example the following name formed by the application of the nesting order rules given above results in the appearance of consecutive parentheses twice.2-{2-\[(1-ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl)amino]propanoyl}-1,2,3,4-tetrahydroisoquinoline-3-carboxylic acid (without stereochemistry)\
(3_S_)-2-\[(2_S_)-2-{\[(2_S_)-1-ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl]amino}propanoyl]-1,2,3,4-tetrahydroisoquinoline-3-carboxylic acid (with stereochemistry) [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html)With this example the stereochemistry needs to be inserted at three positions. Insertion of the third one into the name without stereochemistry results in two opening parenthesis next to each other. Hence to clarify the brackets these need to be adjusted as shown by the second name.

Explanation: The order of insertion of stereochemistry for 2-{2-\[(1-ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl)amino]propanoyl}-1,2,3,4-tetrahydroisoquinoline-3-carboxylic acid is as shown below.

> Stage 1 insert stereochemistry at the inner most position:
>
> 2-{2-{\[(2_S_)-1-ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl]amino}propanoyl}-1,2,3,4-tetrahydroisoquinoline-3-carboxylic acid
>
> The substituent (2_S_)-1-ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl requires square brackets to surround it hence subsequent enclosing marks need to be adjusted.
>
> Stage 2 insert stereochemistry at the next position:
>
> 2-\[(2_S_)-2-{\[(2_S_)-1-ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl]amino}propanoyl]-1,2,3,4-tetrahydroisoquinoline-3-carboxylic acid
>
> The substituent (2_S_)-2-{\[(2_S_)-1-ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl]amino}propanoyl has a parenthesis on the left and brace on the right so to make clear it requires square brackets around it.
>
> Stage 3 insert stereochemistry at the third position:
>
> (3_S_)-2-\[(2_S_)-2-{\[(2_S_)-1-ethoxy-1-oxo-4-phenylbutan-2-yl]amino}propanoyl]-1,2,3,4-tetrahydroisoquinoline-3-carboxylic acid

| This procedure is a change to alleviate the situation that can happen when one follows precisely the nesting order given above and it is necessary to insert independent enclosing marks to accommodate other factors, such as stereodescriptors, that two or more enclosing marks of the same type might line up consecutively resulting in confusion. |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |

P-16.6 ITALICIZATION
