Italicizing marks letters that are not involved in the primary stage of alphanumerical ordering. In manuscripts, italics are conventionally indicated by underlining when an italic font is not available.

P-16.6.1 Lower case italic letters are used in descriptors for fusion sites in names of fused ring systems.

Example:

selenopheno\[2,3-_b_]selenophene (PIN, [P-25.3.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030103))The letters _o_, _m_, and _p_ have been used in place of _ortho_, _meta_, and _para_, respectively, to designate the 1,2-, 1,3-, and 1,4- isomers of disubstituted benzene. This usage is strongly discouraged and is not used in preferred IUPAC names.

Example:

_o_-xylene ([P-22.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#220103))\
1,2-xylene (PIN)\
1,2-dimethylbenzeneP-16.6.2 Italicized elements symbols, such as _O_, _N_, _As_, are locants indicating attachment of a substituent to these heteroatoms

Examples:

_N_,_N_-diethylethanamine (PIN, [P-62.2.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#62020201))

_O_-ethyl hexaneselenoate (PIN, [P-65.6.3.3.7.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#650603030701))

P-16.6.3 The italic element symbol H denotes indicated or added hydrogen.

Examples:

1_H_-azepine (PIN, [P-22.2.2.1.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2202020104))

quinolin-2(1_H_)-one (PIN, [P-64.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#640301))

P-16.6.4 Italic terms, syllables, and capital Roman letters are used in some structural descriptors and stereodescriptors, such as ‘_cis_’, ‘_trans_’, ‘_R_’, ‘_S_’, ‘_E_’, ‘_Z_’, ‘_r_’, ‘_s_’, ‘_c_’, ‘_t_’, and ‘_retro_’.

Examples:

‘_tert_’, but not ‘iso’ ([P-29.6.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#290603))

‘_E_’ and ‘_Z_’ ([P-93.4.2.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#9304020101)); ‘_cis_’, and ‘_trans_’ ([P-93.4.2.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#9304020101)); ‘_r_’, ‘_c_’, and ‘_t_’ ([P-93.5.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#93050103));

‘_R_’ and ‘_S_’ ([P-93.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#930101)), ‘_R\*_’ (spoken R-star), ‘_S\*_’ (spoken S-star), ‘_r_’, ‘_s_’, ([P-93.5.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#93050101)), ‘_rel_’ ([P-93.1.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#93010201))

‘_meso_’ ([P-102.5.6.5.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P10.html#10205060502)), ‘_ambo_’ ([P-93.1.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#930104)), ‘_rac_’ ([P-93.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#930103))

‘_M_’ and ‘_P_’, ‘_R_a’ and ‘_S_a’, ‘_R_p’ and ‘_S_p’ ([P-93.4.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#93040202) and [P-93.5.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#93050501))

‘_TPY_-3’, ‘_TS_-3’, ‘_SS_-4’, ‘_TBPY_’, ‘_SPY_’, and ‘_OC_’ ([P-93.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P9.html#9303))

‘_retro_’, but not ‘abeo’, ‘apo’, ‘cyclo’, ‘de’, ‘des’, ‘homo’, ‘nor’ or ‘seco’ ([P-101.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P10.html#1010301) through [P-101.3.7](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P10.html#1010307))

P-16.7 ELISION OF VOWELS

P-16.7.1 Vowels are systematically elided as follows:

> (a) the terminal letter ‘e’ in names of parent hydrides or endings ‘ene’ and ‘yne’ when followed by a suffix or ‘en’ ending beginning with ‘a’, ‘e’, ‘i’, ‘o’, ‘u’, or ‘y’;
>
> Examples:
>
> pentanal (PIN, [P-66.6.1.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6606010101))
>
> cyclopentadec-1-en-4-yne (PIN, [P-31.1.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P3.html#31010301))
>
> methanium (PIN, [P-73.1.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#73010102))
>
> butan-2-one (PIN, [P-64.2.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#64020201))
>
> tetramethylboranuide (PIN, [P-72.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P7.html#7203))
>
> sulfanyl (preselected prefix, [P-29.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#290301))
>
> (b) in Hantzsch-Widman names, the final letter ‘a’ of an ‘a’ prefix when followed by a vowel;
>
> Examples:
>
> 1,3-thiazole (PIN, [P-22.2.2.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2202020103))\
> (not 1,3-thiaazaole)
>
> 1,6,2-dioxazepane (PIN, [P-22.2.2.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2202020103))\
> (not 1,6,2-dioxaazaepane)
>
> (c) the terminal letter ‘a’ in the names of numerical multiplicative prefixes when followed by a suffix beginning with ‘a’ or ‘o’;
>
> Examples:
>
> \[1,1′-biphenyl]-3,3′,4,4′-tetramine (PIN, [P-62.2.4.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6202040102))\
> (not \[1,1′-biphenyl]-3,3′,4,4′;-tetraamine)
>
> benzenehexol (PIN, [P-63.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#630102))\
> (not benzenehexaol)
>
> (d) the terminal letter ‘a’ of an element ‘a’ prefix in ‘a(ba)_n_’ repeating unit names when followed by a vowel;
>
> Examples:
>
> disiloxane (preselected name, [P-21.2.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#21020301))\
> (not disilaoxane)
>
> tetrastannoxane (preselected name, [P-21.2.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#21020301))\
> (not tetrastannaoxane)
>
> (e) the terminal letter ‘o’ of a functional replacement infix when followed by a vowel;
>
> Example:
>
> _N_,_P_-diphenylphosphonochloridimidic acid (PIN, [P-67.1.2.4.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#670102040101))\
> (not _N_,_P_-diphenylphosphonochloridoimidic acid)(f) the terminal letter ‘o’ of ‘benzo’ in names of ‘benzoheterocycles’ formed by fusion of a benzene ring to a heteromonocycle whose name begins with a vowel \[an exception to [P-16.7.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160702) (g)].3-benzoxepine (PIN, [P-25.2.2.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25020204))
>
> 4_H_-3,1-benzoxazine (PIN, [P-25.2.2.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25020204))

P-16.7.2 There is no elision of terminal vowels in the following cases:

> (a) in conjunctive names;
>
> Example:
>
> benzeneacetic acid ([P-15.6.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15060101))\
> \[phenylacetic acid (PIN)]\(b) from replacement or numerical multiplicative prefixes in skeletal replacement (‘a’) nomenclature;
>
> Example:
>
> 2,4,6,8-tetrasilaundecan-11-yl (preferred prefix, [P-15.4.3.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#1504030202))(c) from multiplicative prefixes in homogeneous acyclic parent hydrides other than hydrocarbons and boron hydrides;
>
> Example:
>
> nonaazane ([P-21.2.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#210202))\
> (not nonazane)(d) from numerical multiplicative prefixes in multiplicative parent compounds;
>
> Example:
>
> 2,2′,2′′,2′′′-(ethane-1,2-diyldinitrilo)tetraacetic acid\
> _N_,_N_′-(ethane-1,2-diyl)bis\[_N_-(carboxymethyl)glycine(e) from numerical multiplicative prefixes before substituent prefix names;
>
> Example:
>
> 5,6,7,8-tetraiodo-1,2,3,4-tetrahydroanthracene-9-carboxylic acid (PIN, see [P-65.1.2.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#650102040101))(f) from component prefixes of compound (see [P-29.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#290102)) and complex (see [P-29.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#290103)) prefixes before following prefixes beginning with a vowel;
>
> Examples:
>
> chloroamino (preselected name, [P-35.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P3.html#350301))
>
> aminooxy (preselected name, [P-68.3.1.1.1.5](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#680301010105))
>
> (g) from prefixes designating attached components in fusion nomenclature; for example, the terminal letter ‘o’ of acenaphtho, benzo, perylo, phenanthro, and the terminal letter ‘a’ of anthra, cyclopropa, cyclobuta, are not elided before a vowel \[see [P-16.7.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160701) (f) for an exception involving ‘benzo’].

| This recommendation is in accordance with [P-25.3.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030103) and Rule R-2.4.1.1 of the 1993 Guide ([ref. 2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref2)) that abrogated the elision recommended by Rule A-21.4 in the 1979 edition ([ref. 1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref1)). |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |

> Examples:
>
> cyclopropa\[_de_]anthracene (PIN, [P-25.3.8.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#65030801))\
> naphtho\[1,2-_a_]azulene (PIN, [P-25.3.1.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#25030103))

P-16.8 ADDITION OF VOWELS

P-16.8.1 For euphonic reasons, in functional replacement nomenclature the vowel ‘o’ is inserted between consonants.

Examples:

ethanesulfonodiimidic acid (PIN, [P-65.3.1.4](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#65030104))\
(not ethanesulfondiimidic acid)

phenylphosphononitridic acid (PIN, [P-67.1.2.4.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#670102040101))\
(not phenylphosphonnitridic acid)

P-16.8.2 For euphonic reasons, the letter ‘a’ is inserted between the root of the name for polyenes, polyynes, and polyenynes, and the numerical multiplicative prefix ‘di’, ‘tri’, etc., preceding the ending ‘ene’ or ‘yne’.

Examples:

buta-1,3-diene (PIN, [P-31.1.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P3.html#31010102))\
(not but-1,3-diene)

hexa-1,3-dien-5-yne (PIN, [P-31.1.2.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P3.html#3101020201))\
(not hex-1,3-dien-5-yne)

P-16.9 PRIMES

In preferred IUPAC names, primes, double primes, etc., sometimes with superscripted arabic numbers that are the locants of the parent structure to which a group is attached, are added to locants and symbols without a space and are not italicized even after italic fonts. When more than three primes are required, they are cited in group of threes.

P-16.9.1 Primes (′), double primes (′′), triple primes (′′′), etc. are used to differentiate the nitrogen atoms of hydrazides ([P-66.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#6603)), imidamides (amidines) (see [P-66.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#660401)), hydrazonamides (amidrazones) (see [P-66.4.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#660402)), and hydrazonohydrazides (hydrazidines) (see [P-66.4.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#660403)).

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609a.gif)\
_N_′-acetyl-_N_′-ethyl-_N_-methylbutanehydrazide (PIN, [P-66.3.3.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66030302))

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609b.gif)\
pentanehydrazide (PIN, [P-66.3.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66030101))

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609c.gif)\
hexanimidamide (PIN, [P-66.4.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66040101))\
(no longer hexanamidine)

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609d.gif)\
benzenecarbohydrazonamide (PIN, [P-66.4.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66040201))

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609e.gif)\
butanehydrazonohydrazide (PIN, [P-66.4.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#66040301))

P-16.9.2 Superscript arabic numbers, which are the locants of the parent structure, are used to differentiate the nitrogen atoms of di- and polyamines, di- and polyimines, di- and polyamides, except for geminal amines, imines, and amides.

| Superscript arabic numbers are now used to differentiate the nitrogen atoms of symmetrical diamines, diimines, diamides, di(imidamides), di(amidines), di(hydrazonamides), di(amidrazones), di(hydrazonohydrazides), imidohydrazides, and polyimidopolycarbonic and inorganic oxoacids, where primes (′), double primes (′′), triple primes (′′′), etc. were formerly used. |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609f.gif)\
_N_1-ethyl-_N_2-methylethane-1,2-diamine (PIN, [P-62.2.4.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6202040102))\
_N_-ethyl-_N_′-methylethane-1,2-diamine

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609g.gif)\
_N_1,_N_4-dimethylnaphthalene-1,4-diimine (PIN, [P-62.3.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#62030101))\
_N_,_N_′-dimethylnaphthalene-1,4-diimine (see also [P-58.2.2.3](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P5.html#58020203))\
_N_,_N_′-dimethyl-1,4-dihydronaphthalene-1,4-diimine

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609h.gif)\
_N_1,_N_5-dimethylpentanediamide (PIN, [P-66.1.1.3.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6a.html#660101030101))\
_N_,_N_′-dimethylpentanediamide

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609i.gif)\
_N_4,2-dimethylpentane-2,4-diamine (PIN, [P-62.2.4.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6202040102))

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609j.gif)\
1,3-diimidodicarbonic acid (PIN, [P-65.2.3.1.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#650203010201))

Superscript arabic numbers are also used to differentiate the chalcogen atoms in polynuclear organic and inorganic oxoacids.

| The use of superscripted letter locants is a change from previous practice where numerical locants were placed in front of the letter locants such as 1-_O_ and 3-_O_, as described in [ref. 1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref1), Rule C-213.1. |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |

Example:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609k.gif)\
1,3-dithiodicarbonic _S_1,_S_3-acid\
(not 1,3-dithiodicarbonic 1-_S_,3-_S_-acid)P-16.9.3 Primes (′), double primes (′′), triple primes (′′′), etc., with superscripted numerical locants indicating the position of the suffix on the parent structure, are used to differentiate the nitrogen atoms in cases other than those listed in [P-16.9.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160901) and [P-16.9.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#160902), above, especially when symmetry conditions are not fulfilled.

Examples:

![](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1gif/P1609l.gif)\
_N_3-ethyl-_N_′3-methylhexane-3,3-diamine (PIN, [P-62.2.4.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P6.html#6202040102))\

P-16.9.4 Primes (′), double primes (′′), triple primes (′′′), etc., are also used to differentiate identical locants other than _N_ locants, for example 1, 1′, 1′′, 4′a (not 4a′; for locants of a fused ring component, [![error details](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/greek/ALTER.GIF)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/changes.html) primes are added after the number, not after the letter). Such usage occurs:

> (a) in multiplicative nomenclature to denote multiplied units and modify locants accordingly;
>
> Example:
>
> 2,2′,2′′-nitrilotri(ethan-1-ol) (PIN, [P-15.3.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P1.html#15030201))(b) in spiro-fused compounds, to denote positions in polycyclic systems, identical or different;
>
> Examples:
>
> 7,7′-spirobi\[bicyclo\[4.1.0]heptane] (PIN, [P-24.3.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#240301))
>
> 1_H_,1′_H_,1′′_H_,3′_H_-2,2′:7′,2′′-dispiroter\[naphthalene] (PIN, [P-24.4.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#240401))
>
> spiro\[cyclohexane-1,1′-indene] (PIN, [P-24.5.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#240501))
>
> (c) in ring assemblies, to number identical ring components;
>
> Examples:
>
> 1,1′-bi(cyclopropane) (PIN, [P-28.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#280201))
>
> 1,1′-biphenyl (PIN, [P-28.2.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#280201))
>
> 3a,3′a-biindene (PIN, [P-28.2.3)](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#280203)

P-16.9.5 Primes also occur:

> (a) in fusion nomenclature, to identify first and higher attached components, identical attached components, and multiparent names;
>
> Examples:
>
> pyrido\[1′′,2′′:1′,2′]imidazo\[4′,5′:5,6]pyrazino\[2,3-_b_]phenazine (PIN, [P-25.3.4.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2503040101))
>
> difuro\[3,2-_b_:2′,3′-_e_]pyridine (PIN, [P-25.3.4.1.2](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#2503040102))
>
> cyclopenta\[1,2-_b_:5,1-_b_′]bis(\[1,4]oxathiine) (PIN, [P-25.3.7.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#250701))
>
> (b) in fullerenes _ortho_-fused to organic ring or ring systems, to identify positions in the nonfullerene component;
>
> Example:
>
> 3′_H_-cyclopropa\[1,9]\(C60-_I_h)\[5,6]fullerene (PIN, [P-27.6.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P2.html#270601))(c) in natural product nomenclature, to identify positions in ring(s) fused to a fundamental parent hydride;
>
> Example:
>
> naphtho\[2′,1′:2,3]-5α-androstane ([P-101.5.1.1](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/P10.html#101050101))

P-16.9.6 Multiple primes

Long strings of primes may be needed with ring assemblies and polyspiro compound. It is difficult to count long streams of primes. For example, how many primes appear in this string: ′′′′′′′′ ? It is eight. In these recommendations, to simplify the counting process, long strings of primes are broken into groups of three as: ′′′ ′′′ ′′, which has the same number of primes as the string above. This is a change from the publication on spiro compounds ([ref. 8](https://iupac.qmul.ac.uk/BlueBook/refs.html#ref8)) in which multiple primes were separated by a space after every four primes.
